## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (constitutive modeling with thermal effects)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which strongly indicates a constitutive law identification problem in solid mechanics/materials science. Common relationships include elastic/plastic stress–strain laws with temperature-dependent modulus, yield stress softening with temperature, and thermomechanical coupling (thermal strain and thermoelastic stress).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (temperature-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (small-strain elasticity with stiffness changing with temperature)
- Hooke + thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (1D thermoelasticity with coefficient of thermal expansion absorbed into c1)
- Quadratic elastic nonlinearity (Landau/Murnaghan-like 1D): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 (moderate-strain elastic nonlinearity at fixed T)
- Temperature-modulated nonlinear elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2 (nonlinear stress–strain with thermal softening/stiffening)
- Hyperelastic polynomial (Mooney-Rivlin-like 1D proxy): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**3 (rubbery/large-strain stiffening behavior in 1D surrogate form)
- Exponential strain hardening: sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1) (rapid hardening at larger strain, e.g., polymers/foams surrogate)
- Thermally activated modulus (exponential softening): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (effective stiffness changing exponentially with temperature over a range)
- Johnson–Cook-type flow stress (reduced form): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (plastic hardening with multiplicative thermal softening factor)
- Power-law hardening with thermal prefactor: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (plastic/creep-like scaling with temperature dependence)
- Ramberg–Osgood inverted surrogate (stress as function of strain): sigma = c0 * (epsilon / (c1 + epsilon))**c2 (smooth transition from linear to nonlinear response; useful surrogate even when derived from implicit form)
- Thermal yield drop + post-yield hardening (smooth): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * tanh(c3 * epsilon) (captures an initial linear regime plus saturation/transition in flow contribution)
- Piecewise elastoplastic with thermal yield (structural form): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - Max(epsilon - (c1 + c2 * T), 0)) + (c3 + c4 * T) * Max(epsilon - (c1 + c2 * T), 0) (elastic slope then reduced/increased tangent modulus after a T-dependent yield strain)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent stiffness → multiply epsilon by a T-dependent factor such as (c0 + c1 * T) or exp(c0 + c1 * T).
- Thermal expansion-induced stress offset (if strain includes thermal part) → use sigma depending on (epsilon - c * (T - c0)) rather than epsilon alone.
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → introduce smooth/implicit switching via tanh(c*epsilon), epsilon/(c+epsilon), or explicit Max(epsilon - epsilon_y(T), 0).
- Strain hardening vs. softening → add higher powers of epsilon (hardening) or saturating functions (softening/plateau) to the baseline linear term.
- Thermal softening of strength → make the plastic/flow contribution multiply by a decreasing function of T (often linear in T over a limited range, or exponential in T).
- Large-strain stiffening (e.g., polymers) → odd high-order terms like epsilon**3 or exp(c*epsilon) added to linear elasticity.
- Near-zero stress at zero strain constraint → prefer forms with sigma=0 when epsilon=0 unless an explicit thermal/pre-stress offset is physically intended.
- Dimensional consistency cue → sigma typically scales like (modulus)×epsilon, so many plausible models look like epsilon times a temperature-dependent modulus plus nonlinear corrections in epsilon.

\[
(T-352.1579)\Big(-0.5449782742+1.5180288401\,\epsilon^{0.6261602092}\Big)

Expand into “\(T\)-part + constant-in-\(T\) part”:
\[
T\Big(-0.5449782742+1.5180288401\,\epsilon^{0.6261602092}\Big)\;+\;352.1579\Big(0.5449782742-1.5180288401\,\epsilon^{0.6261602092}\Big)

\[
T\cdot A \;+\; T\cdot B\,\epsilon^{p}\;+\; C \;+\; D\,\epsilon^{p}
\]
with **no** plain \(\epsilon\) term, no other nonlinearities, and \(p=0.6261602092\). Also GT uses \(\epsilon^p\); candidates often use \(|\epsilon|^p\), which is equivalent on the plausible domain \(\epsilon\ge 0\).

Now check candidates.

1) Has extra rational terms \(T*c3/(c4\epsilon+c5)\) and \(c8/(c4\epsilon+c5)\) and a linear \(\epsilon\) term. Can set those coefficients to 0, leaving \(T c0 + T c1|\epsilon|^{c2} + c7|\epsilon|^{c2}+c9\). This can match GT (choose \(c2=p\), \(\epsilon\ge0\), and fit coefficients). **Match possible.**

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$-c_0(T - c_1) + \epsilon^{c_2} \cdot c_3 \cdot (T - c_4)$$

With c1 = c4 = 352.1579..., so:
$$-c_0(T - c_1) + c_3 \cdot \epsilon^{c_2} \cdot (T - c_1)$$
$$= (T - c_1)(-c_0 + c_3 \cdot \epsilon^{c_2})$$

Expanding:
$$= -c_0 T + c_0 c_1 + c_3 T \epsilon^{c_2} - c_3 c_1 \epsilon^{c_2}$$

So the GT has the form:
$$\alpha T + \beta T \epsilon^{c_2} + \gamma \epsilon^{c_2} + \delta$$

where:
- α = -c₀ = -0.5450
- β = c₃ = 1.5180
- γ = -c₃c₁ = -534.47
- δ = c₀c₁ = 191.92
- c₂ = 0.6262

The basis functions are: {T, T·ε^p, ε^p, 1} where p ≈ 0.6262.

**Key structural requirement:** The GT has exactly these 4 terms with basis functions {T, T·ε^p, ε^p, 1}. No epsilon (linear), no other functions.

Now I'll check each candidate. Under the domain constraint, ε ≥ 0, so |ε| = ε and Abs(epsilon)^c = epsilon^c.

For a candidate to match, it must be expressible with exactly the basis functions {T, T·ε^p, ε^p, 1} (with p free). Any extra basis functions that can't be zeroed out or absorbed make it a NO MATCH.
